Strengtheningthe Fiduciary Framework

Public Procurement Reform

51.     As mentioned above, implementation o f the PERAC has led to improvement in
procurement speed and transparency. The procurement lags were reduced from 8 months in2000
to 4 months in 2002 (the goal was five months by 2003). Twice a week since January 31,2003,
the government has published all the calls for bidding, evaluation reports o f bids, and contract
awards relatedto public procurement inthe public procurement journal.

52.     The government will implement five recommendations o f the national workshop held in
2002, to improve procurement performance: (i)strengthen the institutional and legal framework,
to improve and add autonomy to the system; (ii)modernize procurement procedures; (iii)
reinforce procurement capacities; (iv) put in place an independent control system; and (v) apply
o f adequate measures to fight corruption. The plan o f action for short-, medium-, and long-term
reform o fprocurementmechanisms was adopted by the Council o fMinisters inDecember 2003.

53.     To improve the legal and institutional framework, the government has submitted to the
National Assembly a draft law modifying the institutional framework in the current procurement
code, creating a national agency for the regulation o fprocurement.

54.     The government plans to: (i)establish the national regulatory agency; (ii)      establish a
National Public Procurement Directorate; and (iii)set up Procurement Units in the sector
ministries. The plan o f action for procurement reform includes measures to guarantee the full
functioning and competent staffing o f these entities throughout the next 12 months. Inaddition,
the plan o f action will include anti-corruption measures in the procurement code, in line with the
Government's anti-corruption program.


Imurove FinancialManagement t: StrengthenBudget Management and Government Accounting

55.     The computerized system o f budget management (SIGFIP) introduced in 2001 does not
yet provide data on an actual-time basis on: (i)the overall rate o f execution o f the budget; (ii)
execution rates for line ministries; or (iii)detailed execution rates o f sector programs.       In
addition, SIGFIP does not keep track o f government revenues.

56.     With respect to public accounting, all payment orders issued through the SIGFIP are
entered manually into the computerized Treasury accounts management system (WMONEY),
due to the lack o f interface between the two systems. This practice is the source o f errors and
delays. The weak control on carry-over credits can also create delays. Inorder to remedy these
problems, a global plan was put in place to computerize the Treasury Accounts (ASTER) and
establish an operational interface with SIGFIP by the end o f 2004.

57.     The measures to be implementedare based on:

             e   Expanding the SIGFIP functionality to generate more reliable and complete
                 financial data on the implementation o f the budget.

            0     Full integration of all commitments on budgeted expenditures in this
                  computerized expenditure management system.

Reform and Rationalization of Internal Control andAudit

58.     The current budgetary reform and the implementation of a results-based management
system call for a transformation of intemal control of public administration. The organization
and methods o f internal control must adapt to support the performance of government programs
while mitigating the risks of mismanagement, Each intemal control unit and its activities for the
last three years have been carefully reviewed, to lay the foundations for the development of a
global reform program. Such a program will be implemented starting in June 2004 by the
adoption by the Council of Ministers of a decree: (i)      clarifying the organization and attributions
of internal audit bothat the level of line ministries and the overall government, and (ii)   norms and
standards in order to ensure an effective internal control consistent with result-based
management. The program will first restructure internal control functions, regrouping them in a
single intemal control unit in each ministryto be inplace by December 2004. The program will
thenextend the restructuringand establish a single control unit with nation-wide competency, by
December 2005.

59.     A working group will be responsible for development, planning, and preparation of the
reform program and its operational modalities, by June 2004. The working group will follow the
following principles: (i)   simplicity of organization of the control function; (ii) o f control
                                                                                        unity
within each ministry and on the national level; and (iii)    professional, but not hierarchal, relations
between The General Finance Inspectorate (Inspection G&n&ruZedes Finances) and the other
control units (norms, standards and practices). Technical support will be provided to The General
Finance Inspectorate to develop a training program for the practice of control in a results-based
management system.

60.     The government will monitor progress inreform of the fiduciary framework with several
quantitative performance indicators: (i)    the procurement lags; (ii) payments lags; (iii)the
                                                                           the
publication of contract awards related to public procurement; (iv) the budget execution rate; (v)
the preparation o f quality budget execution reports. Targets for those indicators were set by
agreement with the extemal development partners, with reference to accomplishments in 2003.
The measures indicated in this Letter of Development Policy should translate into continued
improvement in the overall budget management indicators, as shown in the Table o f Indicators
attached to this letter.

audit reports prepared by the Chamber of Accounts of 2001program-budget implementation for
7 pilot ministries were submitted to the National Assembly. Inorder to systematically expand
performance audits to all ministries engaged inreform, the Government will increase the staffing
o f the Chamber of Accounts. With current staffing, the Chamber of Accounts will continue
performance audits on the pilot ministries, focusing its efforts in the education sector on the
Primary and Secondary Education Ministry. As the number of auditors increase, performance
audits will be extended to other sector ministries engaged in the reform, based on the timetable
established by the Chamber of Accounts. The Government's objective i s to expand to 3 additional
ministries in 2004, 5 in2005, and 2 in2006. At the least, staffing o f the Chamber must allow the
extension o f performance audits to the Ministryof Mines, Energy, and Water in 2004 and to the
Ministry of Justice and Human Rights in 2006. The timetable will take in account staffing and
resources in the Chamber of Accounts and will seek to produce the year Naudit report no later
than December of the year N+lby 2006 for all sector ministries engagedinthe reform.

63.     The Chamber of Accounts intends to audit government accounts and comply with the
timetable in the Memorandum of Understanding between the Government and the IDA''. Inline
with the timetable, the Chamber o f Accounts seeks to: (i) up on auditing; (ii)
                                                                 catch                          combine
performance audit with financial audit in preparing budget execution reporting law (Loi de
Rzglement); and (iii) produce the report for the year Nno later than December of the year N+lby
2005. In addition, the objective o f the Chamber of Accounts is to extend auditing to local
governments (Communes) in 2004, to conduct management audits of selected public entities and
public enterprises, and initiate sanction procedures where mismanagement i s identified. The
Chamber of Accounts also plans to conduct jurisdictional control over accounts of certain public
accountants (if it has the necessary capacities) and to verify accounts for the presidential
campaign of 2006.

64.     Inorder to carry out these activities which require a reinforcement of capacities inthe
Chamber of Accounts, necessary means will be usedto allow it to pursue the development o f its
capacities with regardto performance audits and to update its auditing methods.

Decentralization

65.     The government will pursue the process of decentralization, following the first municipal
elections held in December 2002. The budget for 2004 includes a global appropriation o f 3.6
billion CFA francs for local governments, and additional credits of 58 billion CFA francs, to be
managed at the central level. To facilitate the devolution of management responsibilities for
these credits, studies on the modalities and the cost of transfers o f competence to the local
governments are beingfinalized. These studies will be serve as a basis for developing an action
planthat will identify the necessaryimplementation measures andtheir timetable. The legislation
governing the budget and accounting framework of local govemments i s being adopted. Finally,

The Fight Against Corruption

66.      Inorder to promote good govemance andto enhancethe rule of law, the govemment has
adopted a strategic plan for fighting corruption. Its pillars are: (i)revitalizing the system o f
control by passing an anti-corruption law; (ii)promoting of administrative and institutional
reforms; (iii)reinforcing the capacity for action in civil society and in the private sector; (iv)
creating an environment discouraging corruption; and (v) enforcing accountability and fighting
impunity. The programwill seek to consolidate gains inthis area by: (i)  adopting in2004 the law
creating the Anti-Corruption Observatory and granting it logistical resources; (ii)  conducting in
2004 the first survey on govemance and corruption, which will establish the baseline data to
monitor progress in implementing the Anti-Corruption Strategic Plan (PSAC) and to update it in
2005; and (iii)setting up a public information system on the PSAC implementation and
monitoring progress incurbingcorruption.

Arrangements for       the coordination of     the PRSC program, and for monitoring its
implementation and impact

Coordination of the PRSC-supported program

67.      The Program will be coordinated by the Ministry of Finance and Economy through an
inter-ministerial Committee chaired by the Minister o f Finance and Economy. The committee
includes all sectoral Ministries which are responsible for the implementation of the PRSC-
supported program and all Ministers directly involved in cross-sector reform program
implementation. The committee's secretariat will assigned to the Permanent Secretariat of the
National Committee for Development and the FightAgainst Poverty (ST-CNDLP).

Monitoringof the implementationof the PRSC-supported program

68.      Inpractice, capacity for monitoring and evaluation remains weak, and when they exist
are limited to the supervision of budget execution, sector activities, and physical outputs, rather
than on the final results, economic impact, or effectiveness of expenditure programs. The
government will take the following steps to strengthen the monitoring and evaluation capacities
of the sector ministries in each priority sector or sub-sector: (i)complete a list o f pertinent and
realistic performance indicators; (ii)
                                     staff the monitoring and evaluation units o f sector ministries
with appropriate human resources; (iii) inplace systems for measuring performance; and (iv)
                                         set
implement the monitoring and evaluation capacity buildingprogram. For 2004, the govemment
agreedwith IDA on annual target values for monitoring indicators for 2004-2006, for rural water,
public health, basic education, urban environment and sanitation, and forest management, as
indicatedinthe 2004-2006 programbudgets (see Annex 2).

69.      Finally, the PRSC execution will be monitored through reports on the execution of
Program budgets for priority sectors, as well as through reports on the progress o f thematic
reforms.   The government will conduct annual sector reviews jointly with the development
partners. All parties to the programwill maintainregular dialogue with each other.

Monitoring the social impact and poverty inthe PRSC-supported program

70.     When the PRSP was prepared and the systemfor monitoring and evaluating it was set up,
the Government and its development partners recognized the need to create a program to assess
the poverty and social impact o f policies and reforms under the PRSP (PSIA). The responsibility
for identifying, in a participative manner, the areas which would need a PSIA i s included inthe
mandate of the PRSP monitoring and evaluation unit, which i s part o f the Permanent Secretariat
o f the National Commission for Development and Poverty Reduction located in the Ministry of
Finance and Economy.

71.      The first program o f priority studies to be implemented in 2004 will focus on: (i)the
impact of reforms and of the expansion of the cotton sector; (ii)      the low rate of use of health
services; (iii)access for the poor to social services and basic infrastructure; and (iv) the impact of
transfers to schools and local health centers under the HIPC initiative, inparallel with the annual
audit of HIPC expenditures.


Possible evolution o f the PRSC-supported program

72.      The decision to proceed with an eventual second phase, will be based on satisfactory
implementation of the first year of this program and progress in: (i)     the management of public
expenditure; (ii)  access to safe water in rural areas; (iii) performance of the national health
                                                             the
system; and (iv) the quality of basic education. An eventual second phase could broaden the
scope of the program to include other sectors such as Justice, Agriculture, and Rural
Transportation. This evaluation is planned for June 2004.

73.      The government has agreed with IDA that expansion of the PRSC-supported program
will be based on the progress made in the preparation o f these sectors, in particular on the
adoption by the government of: (i)    a realistic operational plan for the integrated reform program
o f legal and judicial systems; (ii)agriculture strategic operation plans; (iii)    an action plan to
reorganize the administrative structure, and human and financial management o f the Ministry o f
Agriculture in order to support successful implementation of the sector strategy; and (iv) a
satisfactory strategy for the development of rural transportation. Throughout the first year of the
program, the government's efforts will focus on preparing the effective implementation of: (i)       a
ten-year reform program of legal and judicial systems; (ii)      a realistic administration and civil
service reformaction plan; and (iii)   apolicy for private sector-led growth.

74.      The government believes that these policies and measuresconstitute an important step for
attaining the medium-term objectives of its PRSP. Therefore it seeks IDA'Sfinancial assistance
to support the implementationo f its poverty reductionstrategy.
